      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n23459-1" target="شَيْبَانُ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n23458"/></foreign>, and sometimes <foreign lang="ar">شِيبَانُ</foreign>, and the latter is as above, (K,) and sometimes <foreign lang="ar">مَلْحَانُ</foreign>, (TA,) <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">The two months of winter;</hi> (A, TA;) [as though meaning <hi rend="ital">the second of the Six Seasons,</hi> commencing two months after the autumnal equinox; (see the former of the two tables in p. 1254;)] <hi rend="ital">i. q.</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">شَهْرَا قِمَاحٍ</foreign>, (S, A, K, TA,) which are <hi rend="ital">the two coldest months;</hi> (S, K, TA;) so called because of the earth's being then white with snow and hoar frost; (S, TA;) <hi rend="ital">falling at the period of the</hi> [<hi rend="ital">auroral</hi>] <hi rend="ital">rising of the Scorpion and the Vulture,</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">العَقْرَب</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">النَّسْر</foreign>, [by which latter is meant <foreign lang="ar">النَّسْرُ الوَاقِعُ</foreign>, i. e. the star a of Lyra,]) <hi rend="ital">said by him who knows not to be the two Kánoons</hi> [i. e. <foreign lang="ar">كَانُونُ الأَوَّلُ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">كَانُونُ الثَّانِى</foreign>, corresponding to December and January O.S.]: (TA:) [it appears that they nearly agree with the two Kánoons; for El-Kazweenee and others say that <foreign lang="ar">القَلْبُ</foreign> (i. e. the heart of the Scorpion, which is the 18th of the Mansions of the Moon,) and <foreign lang="ar">النَّسْرُ الوَاقِعُ</foreign> rise together, and their auroral rising in Central Arabia, about the commencement of the era of the Flight, accord. to my calculation, (see <foreign lang="ar">مَنَازِلُ القَمَرِ</foreign> in art. <foreign lang="ar">نزل</foreign>,) was on the 25th of November O. S.: see also <foreign lang="ar">مِلْحَانُ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">قِمَاحٌ</foreign>: it is also said that] <foreign lang="ar">شِيبَانُ</foreign> [used alone] is a name of [<hi rend="ital">the month</hi>] <foreign lang="ar">كانون الاوّل</foreign>, because of the whiteness of the earth by reason of the hoar-frost and snow. (Mgh.)    </entryFree>2a:T16b1,<entryFree id="n23463" key="أَشْيَبُ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">أَشْيَبُ</orth>

                  <hi rend="ital">White-haired, white-headed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">horary:</hi> (S, A, Mgh, Msb, K:) [it is said to be] anomalous in form; (S, Mgh, Msb;) for an epithet of this measure is only formed [by rule] from a verb of the measure <foreign lang="ar">فَعِلَ</foreign>, aor. <foreign lang="ar">يَفْعَلُ</foreign>; (S, TA;) and it is a condition of the formation of such an epithet that it must denote a defect or the like, or a colour: but <foreign lang="ar">أَشْيَبُ</foreign> signifies <hi rend="ital">white-headed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">hoaryheaded;</hi> [so that it does denote a colour;] and ElKhafájee says that it is reckoned among epithets denoting defects, or blemishes, like <foreign lang="ar">أَعْمَى</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">أَعْرَجُ</foreign>: (MF, TA:) it is said in the K that it has no <foreign lang="ar">فَعْلَآء</foreign>, i. e., (TA,) the epithet <foreign lang="ar">شَيْبَآءُ</foreign> is not applied to a woman; (Msb, TA;) <foreign lang="ar">شَمْطَآءُ</foreign> being used in its stead; (TA;) though one says <foreign lang="ar">شَابَ رَأْسُهَا</foreign>: (Msb, TA:) [but see Har p. 418, where <foreign lang="ar">شَيْبَآءُ</foreign> is mentioned, applied to a woman, as meaning <hi rend="ital">aged,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">white,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">hoary, in the head:</hi> and see <foreign lang="ar">شَيْبَآءُ</foreign> in art. <foreign lang="ar">شوب</foreign>:] the pl. is <foreign lang="ar">شِيبٌ</foreign>; (S, A, Mgh, Msb, K;) with which is syn. <foreign lang="ar">شُيَّبٌ</foreign>; (TA, as from the K; [but not found by me in the copies of the K to <pb n="1628"/> which I have had access;]) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n23463-1" target="شُيُبٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n23456"/></foreign>: (K, TA:) this last is said by IM to be allowable in poetry, <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى التَّمَامِ</foreign> [here meaning as though it were a word composed of sound letters]; and this is the assertion of the lexicologists [in general]: ISd thinks it to be pl. of   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n23463-2" target="شَائِبٌ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n23462"/></foreign> [q. v.], like as <foreign lang="ar">بُزُلٌ</foreign> is of <foreign lang="ar">بَازِلٌ</foreign>; or pl. of   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n23463-3" target="شَيُوبٌ" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n23461"/></foreign> [which app. means <hi rend="ital">very white</hi> or <hi rend="ital">hoary in the head</hi>], accord. to the dial. of the people of El-Hijáz, who say <foreign lang="ar">دَجَاجَةٌ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بَيُوضٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">دَجَاجٌ بُيُضٌ</foreign>. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  [Hence,] one says, <foreign lang="ar">رَأَيْتُ الجِبَالَ شِيبًا</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">I saw the mountains white with snow and hoar frost.</hi> (A, TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">شِيبٌ</foreign> [used alone] signifies <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">Mountains upon which snow falls, and which are white,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">hoary, therewith:</hi> (S, L:) or <hi rend="ital">mountains white with snow</hi> or <hi rend="ital">with dust:</hi> and, some say, <hi rend="ital">white clouds:</hi> sing. <foreign lang="ar">أَشْيَبُ</foreign>. (L, TA.) And, applied to truffles (<foreign lang="ar">كَمْأَة</foreign>), <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">White and large:</hi> (TA:) or simply <hi rend="ital">white.</hi> (Id. voce <foreign lang="ar">تَعَاشِيبُ</foreign>.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">يَوْمٌ أَشْيَبُ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">A day in which are cold and clouds and</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">صُرَاد</foreign> [correctly <foreign lang="ar">صُرَّاد</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">thin clouds,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">cold and humid clouds, in which is no water</hi>]; as also   
      <foreign lang="ar">يَوْمٌ <ref cref="n23463-4" target="شَيْبَانُ" n="4" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n23458"/></foreign>. (K.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">لَيْلَةُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الشَّيْبَآءِ</foreign>, (K,) or <foreign lang="ar">لَيْلَةُ شَيْبَآءَ</foreign>, (TA,) and <foreign lang="ar">لَيْلَةٌ شَيْبَآءُ</foreign>, (TA voce <foreign lang="ar">حُرٌّ</foreign>,) <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">The last night of the</hi> [<hi rend="ital">lunar</hi>] <hi rend="ital">month:</hi> (K, TA:) its first night is called <foreign lang="ar">لَيْلَةُ</foreign>
